[2026-02-16T12:16:36Z] Kartikey Pradhan: In the 1659 treaty, which ended the Franco-Spanish War, Spain agreed to cede 33 villages in the Cerdanya region to the French crown. However, when it came time to hand over Llívia, Spanish negotiators pointed out a technicality: Emperor Charles V had granted Llívia the status of a "villa" (town/city) in the 16th century. ↵ Because the treaty explicitly mentioned the cession of villages, the Spanish argued that Llívia was exempt. The French reluctantly accepted the argument, and the town remains a part of Spain (specifically the province of Girona) to this day, despite being located several kilometers inside French territory.

[2026-02-17T04:23:58Z] Saumay: With answers: ↵ This saga begins with King Z [Charles V], a 16th-century colossus who held the ultimate "Iron Throne" of his era. His dominion was so vast that the phrase "the sun never sets" was first coined for his empire. Though he was the King of A [Spain], he also reigned as the B [Holy Roman] Emperor. Exhausted by the weight of these crowns, he shocked the world by abdicating, enacting a "Grand Split" that divided his house into A [Spanish] and C [Austrian] branches. ↵ The A[Spanish] Branch established its seat in Capital D [Madrid], ruling a global empire of gold and galleons. However, this line withered in 1700, sparking a war that engulfed the world as rival powers fought to claim the vacant throne. Meanwhile, the C[Habsburg] Branch made its home in Capital E [Vienna], building a glittering theater of power that would dictate the culture of the region for centuries. ↵ The family’s survival was tested in the 18th century by Empress Y [Maria Theresa], the dynasty’s only female sovereign. She survived a desperate war of succession and bore 16 children, using them as political glue for the empire. To showcase her global reach, she curated the ‘Millions Room’ in her summer palace at Capital E [Schönbrunn Palace, Vienna], decorating it with rare rosewood and miniatures from the F [Mughal] courts of India, featuring portraits of the emperor X [Shah Jahan]. ↵ In a desperate bid to end three centuries of bloodshed, she orchestrated the ultimate "Diplomatic Revolution" by marrying her daughter, W [Marie Antoinette], to King V [Louis XVI], the ruler of the House of G [Bourbon], the dynasty’s most bitter and ancestral rival. However, this union ended not in peace, but at the foot of the guillotine during the H [French] Revolution. ↵ Out of that revolutionary smoke rose U [Napoleon Bonaparte], a usurper who shattered the old world order. He proved so formidable that T [Francis II], the grandson of Y[Maria Theresa], made a desperate move to protect the dignity of his ancestors. In 1806, T[Francis II] chose to officially dissolve the B [Holy Roman] Empire, permanently extinguishing a crown that had endured for a thousand years. By killing the title himself, he ensured the conqueror could never seize the mantle for his own. To secure a fragile peace, [Francis II] was eventually forced to offer his own daughter [Marie Louise] as a bride to U[Napoleon]. It was a union the usurper craved, for despite his genius, he was an upstart who hungered for the prestige of the C [Habsburg] Dynasty’s ancient "Blue Blood" to legitimize his new regime. ↵ By the mid-19th century, the family faced a new rival, S [Otto von Bismarck], hailing from I [Prussia]. He provoked a lightning-fast war that humiliated the dynasty, excluding them from their ancestral lands forever. Out of this victory, S forged a powerful new empire, J [German Empire], which rose to challenge the old order. Forced to look East to save his crumbling power, Emperor R [Franz Joseph I] reinvented his realm through a historic compromise, transforming his domain into a ‘Dual’ Monarchy that shared power between Capital E [Vienna] and the rising Capital K [Budapest], a move that elevated the Land L [Hungary] to equal status with his own. To project a new image of strength, he celebrated what history remembers as the ‘Wedding of the 19th Century’ to his rebellious, beautiful cousin, P [Elisabeth "Sisi"]. ↵ The dynasty’s long sunset ended with Q [Archduke Franz Ferdinand], the nephew of Emperor Franz Joseph 1, in the early 20th century. Because the Emperor’s only son [Rudolf] had perished in a tragic scandal, the weight of the 600-year-old dynasty fell on Q. What was intended as a routine display of imperial presence in a restive corner of the realm [Sarajevo] became the final curtain call for the age of kings. ‎<This message was edited>

One of the interesting stories about this battle is that the defending Rajput forces equipped their war horses with a peculiar piece of armor: a fake elephant trunk. The idea was that the enemy Y’s war elephants would mistake the horses for baby elephants and instinctively refuse to attack them. Y’s decisive victory in this battle secured Y authority over north India for at least 100 years. ID X and Y.
